The Word 'Yad' in the Quran
Imam Razi cites Quranic verses mentioning God's hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic occurrences of the attribute 'yad' (hand) in both singular and dual forms as cited by Imam Razi.

Core Idea
The Quran uses 'yad' for God in two forms, setting the scriptural foundation for theological debate.

Imam Razi begins his discussion of the divine attribute 'yad' by presenting the scriptural evidence from the Quran. He notes that the word appears in two forms, singular and dual, and cites two specific verses as examples. These verses are foundational for the subsequent debate on how to interpret God's hand.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage introducing the topic
Start by reading the opening statement from Imam Razi where he declares that the word 'yad' appears in both the Quran and hadith, then focus on the Quranic part.
Notice the use of 'اعلم' (Know) to signal important knowledge.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the two verses cited: one from Surah Sad [38:75] using the dual form 'bi-yadayya', and one from Surah al-Ma'ida [5:64] using the dual 'yadahu'. These are presented as examples.
The first verse is in the context of Iblis's refusal to prostrate, the second emphasizes God's generosity.
3
Note the two forms: singular and dual
Imam Razi explicitly says the word occurs in both the singular (wihdan) and dual (tathniya) forms. Recognize that the Quran does not use the plural form for God's hand.
This distinction is important for later theological discussions on multiplicity.
4
Reflect on why Razi starts with the Quran
Consider why the Quranic evidence is presented first. The Quran is the primary source of Islamic theology, so Razi grounds his discussion in revelation before turning to hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السادس عشر
في اليد
اعلم: أن هذه اللفظة وردت في القرآن والأخبار.
أما القرآن: فقد وردت هذه الصيغة بصيغة الوحدان تارة، وبصيغة التثنية أخرى، كقوله تعالى: {ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي} [ص:75]، وقوله: {بل يداه مبسوطتان} [المائدة:64].
وأما الأخبار فكثيرة:
الأول: ما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «التقى آدم وموسى... فقال موسى: أنت الذي خلقك الله بيده، وأسجد لك ملائكته، ونفح فيك من روحه، وأمرك بأمر فعصيته فأخرجك من الجنة. فقال آدم: يا موسى اصطفاك الله بكلامه، وخط لك التوراة بيده. أفتلومني على أمر قد قدره الله علي قبل أن يخلقني بأربعين سنة؟ قال: فحج آدم موسى». وهذا الخبر اشتمل على أن موسى عليه السلام أثبت لله تعالى اليد، وكذلك آدم قال بذلك.
الثاني: روي أبو هريرة رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لما خلق الله تعالى الخلق كتب بيده على نفسه: إن رحمتي سبقت غضبي».
الثالث: روى عبد الله بن عمر عن النبي أنه قال: «إن الله يفتح أبواب السماء في ثلث الليل الباقي فببسط...»
Chapter Sixteen. On the 'yad' (hand). Know that this word occurs in the Qur'an and the hadiths. As for the Qur'an: it occurs in the singular form sometimes, and in the dual form other times, such as His statement: {What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands} [Sad:75], and His statement: {Nay, both His hands are outstretched} [al-Ma'ida:64]. As for the hadiths, they are many. First: what is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Adam and Moses met... Moses said: You are the one whom God created with His hand, and He made His angels prostrate to you, and breathed into you of His spirit, and commanded you to do something but you disobeyed and were expelled from Paradise. Adam said: O Moses, God chose you with His speech and wrote the Torah for you with His hand. Do you blame me for a matter which God decreed upon me before creating me by forty years? He said: So Adam overcame Moses.' This report includes that Moses peace be upon him affirmed the hand of God, and likewise Adam said that. Second: Abu Hurayra narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'When God created the creation, He wrote with His hand upon Himself: My mercy prevails over My wrath.' Third: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'God opens the gates of heaven in the last third of the night and spreads...'
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a collection of textual evidence for the attribute of 'yad' (hand) in the Qur'an and hadith. Imam Razi begins by stating that the word 'yad' appears in both sources. He first cites two Qur'anic verses: one where God says 'with My two hands' (bidadi) and another where He says 'both His hands are outstretched' (yadahu mabsutatani). These are examples of the lone and dual forms. Then he turns to hadith, listing three. The first hadith is the famous debate between Adam and Moses, where both prophets affirm that God created Adam with His hand and wrote the Torah with His hand. Razi notes that this hadith shows both Moses and Adam attributed a hand to God. The second hadith is about God writing with His hand that His mercy precedes His wrath. The third hadith is incomplete in the text as given, mentioning God opening the gates of heaven and spreading something (likely His hand). Razi's purpose is to present the scriptural evidence that the attribute of 'yad' is mentioned, without further interpretation here; he is laying the groundwork for later theological discussion.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
بيدي (bi-yadayya)
يداه (yadahu)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming God's hand implies a physical, human-like hand.
Correction: Imam Razi is only citing the texts. The interpretation of these verses will be discussed later; at this stage, it is simply evidence that the attribute is mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses the attribute 'yad' for God in both singular and dual forms, as shown in Surah Sad and Surah al-Ma'ida.

?
The Quran uses both singular and dual forms for God's hand. Have you ever stopped to consider why both forms are used? What does this diversity teach you about the nature of divine speech? Commit to finding one more verse about God's hand this week.

Hadith Evidence for God's Hand
Imam Razi lists three hadiths that mention God's hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize the hadith evidence for the attribute 'yad' as presented by Imam Razi, including the debate between Adam and Moses.

Core Idea
Hadiths from the Prophet affirm that God has a hand, as seen in the debate between Adam and Moses.

Having presented the Quranic evidence, Imam Razi now turns to the hadith literature. He lists three hadiths that mention God's hand, starting with the famous debate between Adam and Moses where both prophets affirm that God created with His hand and wrote the Torah with His hand. The second hadith speaks of God writing with His hand that mercy precedes wrath. The third hadith is incomplete in the text, mentioning God opening the gates of heaven.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening of the hadith section
Imam Razi transitions from the Quran to the hadith with the phrase 'وأما الأخبار فكثيرة' (As for the hadiths, they are many). This signals that he is now providing prophetic traditions.
2
Examine the first hadith: the debate between Adam and Moses
Read the hadith carefully. Note that both Moses and Adam attribute a hand to God: Moses says 'خلقك الله بيده' (God created you with His hand), and Adam says 'خط لك التوراة بيده' (wrote the Torah for you with His hand). This shows that both prophets affirmed this attribute.
Imam Razi comments that this hadith includes affirmation of the hand by both prophets.
3
Study the second hadith: God writing with His hand
The second hadith from Abu Hurayra states that God wrote with His hand upon Himself: 'إن رحمتي سبقت غضبي' (My mercy prevails over My wrath). This directly attributes writing to God's hand.
This hadith is well-known in discussions of divine mercy.
4
Note the third hadith (incomplete)
The third hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar mentions God opening the gates of heaven and spreading something (likely His hand). The text is cut off, but it is another example of the attribute.
The incompleteness reminds us that this is a manuscript snippet; the full hadith would have more details.

الفصل السادس عشر
في اليد
اعلم: أن هذه اللفظة وردت في القرآن والأخبار.
أما القرآن: فقد وردت هذه الصيغة بصيغة الوحدان تارة، وبصيغة التثنية أخرى، كقوله تعالى: {ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي} [ص:75]، وقوله: {بل يداه مبسوطتان} [المائدة:64].
وأما الأخبار فكثيرة:
الأول: ما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «التقى آدم وموسى... فقال موسى: أنت الذي خلقك الله بيده، وأسجد لك ملائكته، ونفح فيك من روحه، وأمرك بأمر فعصيته فأخرجك من الجنة. فقال آدم: يا موسى اصطفاك الله بكلامه، وخط لك التوراة بيده. أفتلومني على أمر قد قدره الله علي قبل أن يخلقني بأربعين سنة؟ قال: فحج آدم موسى». وهذا الخبر اشتمل على أن موسى عليه السلام أثبت لله تعالى اليد، وكذلك آدم قال بذلك.
الثاني: روي أبو هريرة رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لما خلق الله تعالى الخلق كتب بيده على نفسه: إن رحمتي سبقت غضبي».
الثالث: روى عبد الله بن عمر عن النبي أنه قال: «إن الله يفتح أبواب السماء في ثلث الليل الباقي فببسط...»
Chapter Sixteen. On the 'yad' (hand). Know that this word occurs in the Qur'an and the hadiths. As for the Qur'an: it occurs in the singular form sometimes, and in the dual form other times, such as His statement: {What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands} [Sad:75], and His statement: {Nay, both His hands are outstretched} [al-Ma'ida:64]. As for the hadiths, they are many. First: what is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Adam and Moses met... Moses said: You are the one whom God created with His hand, and He made His angels prostrate to you, and breathed into you of His spirit, and commanded you to do something but you disobeyed and were expelled from Paradise. Adam said: O Moses, God chose you with His speech and wrote the Torah for you with His hand. Do you blame me for a matter which God decreed upon me before creating me by forty years? He said: So Adam overcame Moses.' This report includes that Moses peace be upon him affirmed the hand of God, and likewise Adam said that. Second: Abu Hurayra narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'When God created the creation, He wrote with His hand upon Himself: My mercy prevails over My wrath.' Third: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'God opens the gates of heaven in the last third of the night and spreads...'
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a collection of textual evidence for the attribute of 'yad' (hand) in the Qur'an and hadith. Imam Razi begins by stating that the word 'yad' appears in both sources. He first cites two Qur'anic verses: one where God says 'with My two hands' (bidadi) and another where He says 'both His hands are outstretched' (yadahu mabsutatani). These are examples of the lone and dual forms. Then he turns to hadith, listing three. The first hadith is the famous debate between Adam and Moses, where both prophets affirm that God created Adam with His hand and wrote the Torah with His hand. Razi notes that this hadith shows both Moses and Adam attributed a hand to God. The second hadith is about God writing with His hand that His mercy precedes His wrath. The third hadith is incomplete in the text as given, mentioning God opening the gates of heaven and spreading something (likely His hand). Razi's purpose is to present the scriptural evidence that the attribute of 'yad' is mentioned, without further interpretation here; he is laying the groundwork for later theological discussion.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
بيده (bi-yadihi)
يداه (yadahu)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith in this passage shows both Adam and Moses affirming God's hand?
A) The hadith about God writing mercy over wrath
B) The debate between Adam and Moses
C) The hadith about opening gates of heaven
D) The Qur'anic verse from Sad

Key Takeaway
The hadith evidence includes the Adam-Moses debate, the hadith of mercy, and a hadith about opening heavens, all affirming God's hand.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Adam and Moses both affirmed God's hand without hesitation, do you feel any inner resistance to taking these words at face value? What would it cost you to accept them literally?
?
If the hadith says God wrote 'My mercy prevails over My wrath' with His hand, how should that change the way you approach Him after a sin? Are you truly expecting His mercy to outweigh your failures?
?
The Prophet testified that God opens the gates of heaven and 'spreads' – what does your heart long for Him to spread toward you tonight? Will you ask Him for it with the same certainty that He has a hand to give?

Scriptural Evidence for the Word 'Yad'
Al-Razi enumerates Quranic and hadith evidence for 'yad'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extensive scriptural basis for the term 'yad' (hand) as it appears in the Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
The word 'yad' is firmly rooted in both Quran and Hadith.

Imam al-Razi begins by citing the actual occurrences of the word 'yad' in the Quran and the hadith literature. This passage provides the raw textual evidence before any interpretation, showing that the term is used in both singular and dual forms in the Quran and in numerous prophetic traditions. The hadiths cover a range of contexts, from creation to charity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Notice the two forms: singular (في مَا خَلَقْتُ بِيَدَيَّ) and dual (بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ).
These are the primary scriptural anchors.
2
Study the seven hadiths
Go through each hadith listed by al-Razi, noting the different contexts (creation, law, charity, etc.).
The hadiths are numerous; focus on their diversity.
3
Recognize the abundance
Al-Razi emphasizes that hadiths on this topic are numerous ('كثيرة'). This counters any claim that the term is rare.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask: why does al-Razi list so many examples? To establish that the word is widely used and must be taken seriously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السادس عشر
اعلم : أن هذه اللفظة وردت في القرآن، والأخبار. أما القرآن: فقد وردت هذه الصيغة بصيغة الوحدة تارة، وبصيغة التثنية أخرى كقوله تعالى: (ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي) وقوله: (بل يداه مبسوطتان). وأما الأخبار فكثيرة: الأول: ما روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «التقى آدم وموسى... فقال موسى: أنت الذي خلقك الله بيده، وأسجد لك ملائكته، ونفح فيك من روحه، وأمرك بأمر فعصيته فأخرجك من الجنة. فقال آدم: يا موسى اصطفاك الله بكلامه، وخط لك التوراة بيده. أفتلومني على أمر قد قدره الله علي، قبل أن يخلقني بأربعين سنة؟ قال: فحج آدم موسى. وهذا الخبر اشتمل على أن موسى عليه السلام أثبت لله تعالى اليد، وكذلك آدم قال بذلك. الثاني: روي أن أبا هريرة رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لما خلق الله تعالى الخلق كتب بيده على نفسه: إن رحمتي سبقت غضبي». الثالث: روى عبد الله بن عمر عن النبي أنه قال: «إن الله يفتح أبواب السماء في ثلث الليل الباقي فيبسط يده، فيقول: ألا عبد يسألني فأعطيه، ولا يزال كذلك حتى يطلع الفجر». الرابع: روى أبو هريرة عن النبي أنه قال: «إن أحدكم ليتصدق بالتمرة، إذا كانت من الطيب - ولا يقبل الله إلا طيبا - فيجعلها الله في يده اليمنى. ثم يربيها كما يربي أحدكم فلوه وفصيله، حتى تصير مثل أحد». الخامس: الحديث المشهور، وهو قوله: «إن الصدقة تقع في يد الرحمن، قبل أن تقع في يد الفقير». السادس: ما تواتر النقل عن النبي أنه كان يقول: «والذي نفسي بيده». السابع: قوله عليه السلام: «إن الله خمر طينة آدم بيده أربعين صباحا». والأحاديث في هذا الباب كثيرة.
واعلم: أن لفظ اليد حقيقة في هذه الجارحة المخصوصة، إلا أنه يستعمل على سبيل المجاز، في أمور غيرها: فالأول: إنه يستعمل لفظ اليد في القدرة. يقال: يد السلطان فوق يد الرعية. أي: قدرته غالبة على قدرتهم. والسبب في حسن هذا المجاز: أن كمال حال هذا العضو إنما يظهر بالصفة المسماة بالقدرة. ولما كان المقصود من اليد حصول القدرة، أطلق اسم القدرة على اليد. وقد يقال: هذه البلدة في يد الأمير، وإن كان الأمير مقطوع اليد. ويقال: فلان في يده الأمر والنهي، والحل والعقد. والمراد: ما ذكرناه. والثاني: إن اليد قد يراد بها النعمة. وإنما حسن هذا المجاز، لأن آلة إعطاء النعمة اليد. فإطلاق اسم اليد على النعمة، إطلاق لاسم السبب على المسبب. الثالث: إنه قد يذكر لفظ اليد صلة للكلام على سبيل التأكيد. كقولهم: يداك أوكتا. ويقرب منه: قوله تعالى: (فقدموا بين يدي نجواكم صدقة) وقوله: (بين يدي رحمته) فإن النجوى والرحمة لا يكون لها هذان المضافان المسميان باليدين.
Chapter Sixteen. Know: This word occurs in the Quran and the reports. As for the Quran: this form occurs in the singular form sometimes, and in the dual form other times, like His statement (What prevented you from prostrating to what I created with My two hands) and His statement (But His two hands are outstretched). As for the reports, they are many: First: what is narrated that the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Adam and Moses met... Moses said: You are the one whom God created with His hand, and made His angels prostrate to you, and breathed into you of His spirit, and you disobeyed His command and He expelled you from Paradise. Adam said: O Moses, God chose you with His speech and inscribed the Torah for you with His hand. Do you blame me for a matter which God decreed upon me forty years before He created me? He said: Adam overcame Moses. And this report includes that Moses, peace be upon him, affirmed for God the hand, and likewise Adam said that. Second: It is narrated that Abu Huraira, may God be pleased with him, that the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'When God created creation, He wrote with His hand upon Himself: My mercy precedes My anger.' Third: Abdullah ibn Umar narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'God opens the gates of heaven in the last third of the night and spreads His hand, saying: Is there no servant who asks Me so I give him? And He continues thus until dawn appears.' Fourth: Abu Huraira narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'One of you gives charity with a date, if it is from lawful earnings - and God accepts only what is lawful - and God places it in His right hand, then nurtures it as one of you nurtures his foal and young camel until it becomes like Mount Uhud.' Fifth: The well-known hadith, which is his saying: 'Charity falls into the hand of the Merciful before it falls into the hand of the beggar.' Sixth: What is transmitted successively from the Prophet that he used to say: 'By Him in whose hand is my soul.' Seventh: His saying, peace be upon him: 'God kneaded the clay of Adam with His hand for forty mornings.' And the hadiths on this topic are many. And know: The word 'hand' is literally (haqiqah) for this specific limb, except that it is used metaphorically (majaz) for other things: First: It uses the word 'hand' for power (qudra). It is said: The hand of the ruler is above the hand of the subjects, meaning his power dominates their power. And the reason for the appropriateness of this metaphor is that the perfection of the state of this member appears only by the attribute called power. And since the intended purpose of the hand is the attainment of power, the name of power is applied to the hand. And it may be said: This city is in the hand of the governor, even if the governor has a severed hand. And it is said: So-and-so has in his hand command and prohibition, binding and loosing. And the intended meaning is what we mentioned. Second: The hand may be intended to mean blessing (ni'ma). This metaphor is appropriate because the instrument for giving blessing is the hand. So applying the name of the hand to the blessing is applying the name of the cause to the effect. Third: The word 'hand' may be mentioned as a connective (silah) in speech for emphasis (ta'kid). Like their saying: 'Your hands are tied.' And close to it is His statement: (Present a charity before your confidential talk) and His statement: (Before His mercy), for the confidential talk and mercy do not have these two genitives called hands.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a combined scriptural and linguistic analysis by Imam al-Razi. He begins with the scriptural evidence: first citing Quranic verses that use 'yad' in the singular and dual forms, then enumerating seven hadiths that use the word in various contexts (Adam and Moses, creation, the last third of the night, charity, the soul of the Prophet, and the creation of Adam's clay). After presenting this evidence, he states that the word 'yad' is literally (haqiqah) a specific limb, but it is used metaphorically (majaz) for other meanings. He then explains three metaphorical uses: (1) for 'power' (qudra), giving examples like 'the hand of the ruler' to imply power even if the ruler has no physical hand; (2) for 'blessing' (ni'mah), because the hand is the instrument of giving; (3) as a connective for emphasis (ta'kid) in expressions like 'your hands are tied' and Quranic phrases like 'between the hands of mercy'. The passage carefully preserves the literal meaning while explaining how the same word functions metaphorically, guarding against both anthropomorphism and denial of the scriptural text.

Key Terms
اليد
القرآن
الأخبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only one or two hadiths mention God's hand.
Correction: Al-Razi lists seven distinct hadiths and says they are numerous, showing this is a well-attested term.

Checkpoint
Which of the following hadiths mentions God's right hand?
A) The hadith of Adam and Moses
B) The hadith about charity with a date
C) The hadith about writing mercy
D) The hadith about Oath by the soul

Key Takeaway
The word 'yad' is widely attested in both Quran and Hadith, providing a strong scriptural foundation for discussion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the hadith about God spreading His hand in the last third of the night, do you truly believe He is waiting for you to ask? What fear or laziness keeps you from taking that seriously tonight?
?
The Prophet swore 'by Him in whose hand is my soul' constantly. How often do you live with the awareness that your very existence is held by God? What would change in your next hour if you remembered that?
?
Charity falls into God's hand before the beggar's hand. Does that uncomfortable truth reshape how you give? What is one specific act of giving you can do today as a direct response to that hadith?

Metaphorical Uses of 'Yad'
Al-Razi explains the literal and three metaphorical meanings of 'yad'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three metaphorical uses of the word 'yad' according to Imam al-Razi and how they coexist with the literal meaning.

Core Idea
'Yad' is literal for a limb and metaphorical for power, blessing, and emphasis.

After presenting the scriptural evidence, al-Razi now turns to the linguistic analysis. He affirms that 'yad' is literally a limb, but it also has well-established metaphorical meanings. He identifies three distinct metaphorical uses: power, blessing, and as a connective for emphasis. This analysis allows the believer to accept the scriptural text while avoiding anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Read the literal meaning statement
Al-Razi first states that 'yad' is literally (haqiqah) for a specific limb. This anchors the discussion.
The literal meaning is not denied; it is the basis for metaphor.
2
Examine the first metaphor: power
Note the example 'hand of the ruler' meaning power, even if the ruler is handless. Understand the reasoning: the perfection of the hand is power.
3
Examine the second metaphor: blessing
The hand is the instrument of giving, so it is used for the blessing itself (cause for effect).
4
Examine the third metaphor: emphasis
The word 'yad' can be a connective (silah) for emphasis, as in Quranic phrases like 'between his hands'.
This shows a grammatical function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a combined scriptural and linguistic analysis by Imam al-Razi. He begins with the scriptural evidence: first citing Quranic verses that use 'yad' in the singular and dual forms, then enumerating seven hadiths that use the word in various contexts (Adam and Moses, creation, the last third of the night, charity, the soul of the Prophet, and the creation of Adam's clay). After presenting this evidence, he states that the word 'yad' is literally (haqiqah) a specific limb, but it is used metaphorically (majaz) for other meanings. He then explains three metaphorical uses: (1) for 'power' (qudra), giving examples like 'the hand of the ruler' to imply power even if the ruler has no physical hand; (2) for 'blessing' (ni'mah), because the hand is the instrument of giving; (3) as a connective for emphasis (ta'kid) in expressions like 'your hands are tied' and Quranic phrases like 'between the hands of mercy'. The passage carefully preserves the literal meaning while explaining how the same word functions metaphorically, guarding against both anthropomorphism and denial of the scriptural text.

Key Terms
الحقيقة
المجاز
القدرة
النعمة
التأكيد
الصلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if 'yad' is used metaphorically for God, it can never be literal, or that the literal meaning is entirely negated.
Correction: Al-Razi affirms both the literal and metaphorical uses; the literal meaning remains valid for the limb, while metaphors extend it to other concepts.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, which of the following is NOT one of the three metaphorical uses of 'yad'?
A) Power (qudra)
B) Blessing (ni'ma)
C) Knowledge ('ilm)
D) Emphasis (ta'kid)

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's analysis shows that 'yad' can be literal or metaphorical depending on context, and both are valid interpretations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the phrase 'Yad Allah fawqa aydihim' (The hand of Allah is over their hands), which of Al-Razi's three metaphorical meanings (power, blessing, emphasis) do you naturally assume? Does that assumption shape how you trust Allah's control over your life? How would it change if you focused on a different meaning?
?
Al-Razi notes that even a ruler with a severed hand is said to have 'hand' meaning power. In your own life, when you feel weak or unable, do you still believe that Allah's 'hand' (power) is over your situation? What specific circumstance makes this hard for you, and how can you actively remind yourself of this truth today?
?
If you have ever used the word 'yad' as a mere emphasis (like 'between the hands of mercy'), reflect on a time you recited such a Quranic phrase mindlessly. How can you now make each occurrence of 'yad' in the Quran a moment to consciously consider its intended meaning—whether power, blessing, or emphasis—and let that transform your connection with Allah?

Divine Attributes
beginner
4 min
Four Hadiths on God's Hand from Razi's List
Razi lists four hadiths mentioning God's hand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Razi enumerates several hadiths mentioning God's hand to demonstrate that scriptural texts about divine attributes require interpretation, not literal acceptance.

Core Idea
Scriptural texts about God's hand demand interpretation, not literalism.

Razi presents four hadiths that explicitly mention God's hand. These are drawn from a longer series and serve to show that such expressions are widespread in the prophetic tradition. As you read, consider why a theologian would collect these texts—Razi's purpose is to establish that these texts exist, setting the stage for the need to interpret them metaphorically.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four hadiths
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then note that it starts with the fourth hadith and ends with the seventh, followed by a concluding remark.
The first word 'يده' in the original is a continuation from the previous page; we start from 'الرابع' for clarity.
2
Examine the key phrase in each hadith
For each hadith, find the phrase that mentions God's hand. Notice the different contexts: charity, oath, creation.
The word for hand is 'يد' in various forms.
3
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
A reader might think these hadiths prove God has a literal hand. But Razi is listing them to show they exist and need interpretation.
This aligns with the author's broader project of ta'wil (metaphorical interpretation).
4
Consider why Razi lists multiple hadiths
By presenting several examples, Razi shows that such expressions are not isolated but widespread, strengthening the need for a consistent method of interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يده، فيقول : ألا عبد يسألني فأعطيه ، ولا يزال (1) كذلك حتى يطلع الفجر ، الرابع : روى أبو هريرة عن النبي أنه قال : « إن أحدكم ليتصدق بالتمرة ، إذا كانت من الطيب - ولا يقبل الله إلا طيبا - فيجعلها الله في يده اليمنى. ثم يربيها كما يربى أحدكم فلوه وفصيله ، حتى تصير مثل أحد ، الخامس : الحديث المشهور. وهو قوله : إن الصدقة تقع في « يد الرحمن ، قبل أن تقع في يد الفقير ، السادس : ما تواتر النقل عن النبي أنه كان يقول : « والذي نفسي بيده ، السابع : قوله عليه السلام: إن الله خمر طينة آدم بيده أربعين صباحا ، والأحاديث في هذا الباب : كثيرة
His hand, and He says: 'Is there a servant who asks Me so I may give him?' and He continues like that until dawn. Fourth: Abu Hurairah narrated from the Prophet that he said: 'Indeed one of you gives charity with a date, if it is from good [wealth] – and God accepts only what is good – so God places it in His right hand. Then He nurtures it as one of you nurtures his foal and his young camel, until it becomes like Mount Uhud.' Fifth: The famous hadith, which is his saying: 'Indeed charity falls into the hand of the Merciful before it falls into the hand of the beggar.' Sixth: What has been transmitted successively from the Prophet that he used to say: 'By Whose hand my soul is.' Seventh: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed God kneaded the clay of Adam with His hand for forty mornings.' And the hadiths on this topic are many.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of hadiths from the Prophet that use the word 'hand' (yad) in reference to God. The author lists four specific examples (the fourth to seventh in a longer series) to show that such expressions are widespread in the transmitted tradition. The first two of these hadiths describe God's right hand receiving charity and nurturing it; the third is the common oath formula; the fourth mentions God kneading Adam's clay. The author's purpose is to establish that these scriptural texts exist, so that the reader understands the need for interpretation (ta'wil) since a literal reading would attribute a body part to God.

Key Terms
يد
الصدقة
يد الرحمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These hadiths prove God has a literal hand.
Correction: Razi lists these hadiths to show that they exist and require interpretation, not to assert literalism. The author will later provide metaphorical interpretations.

Checkpoint
How many hadiths are listed in this passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Razi presents four hadiths mentioning God's hand to establish that such scriptural expressions are numerous and require careful interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the hadith 'God places the charity in His right hand', does your mind immediately try to picture a physical hand? What does that reaction reveal about your conception of God? Will you commit to training yourself to interpret such verses metaphorically?
?
If you have ever used the hadith about God kneading Adam's clay with His hand to argue for a literal hand, how does Razi's list challenge that assumption? Are you willing to submit to the scholarly understanding of ta'wil, even if it feels less 'concrete'?
?
The Prophet himself used the phrase 'by Whose hand my soul is'—a common oath. Do you ever use anthropomorphic language about God casually? How can you ensure your words reflect tawhid? What specific change will you make today?
